## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, where stress typically increases nonlinearly with strain (hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening). Classical constitutive models often express these as separable or coupled functions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law with thermal modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening at fixed T)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (separable hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (thermally activated softening)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Swift with thermal: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power-law with exponential thermal softening)
- Polynomial hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial stress-strain relation)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear with saturation)
- Coupled thermal-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart type)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Multiplicative separability: stress often factors as sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), where hardening and thermal softening are independent multiplicative terms
- Strain hardening concavity: stress-strain curves are typically concave down (decreasing hardening rate), suggesting power-law exponents < 1 or saturating exponentials
- Linear thermal softening: many materials show approximately linear decrease of flow stress with temperature over moderate ranges, giving (1 - c*T) or (Tmelt - T) factors
- Exponential thermal activation: at high temperatures, thermally activated processes lead to exp(-c/T) or exp(-c*T) dependence reflecting Boltzmann-type statistics
- Initial yield offset: many constitutive models include an additive constant (yield stress) independent of strain, as in sigma = sigma_y + f(epsilon)
- Strain offset for pre-strain: shifted strain terms like (epsilon + epsilon_0)**n account for initial dislocation density or pre-existing hardening
- Saturation stress: at large strains, stress approaches a finite limit, suggesting forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational fractions in epsilon
- Temperature-dependent hardening rate: the exponent or coefficient in strain hardening may itself depend on T, leading to terms like epsilon**(c0 + c1*T)
